<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">The Ultimate Warrior</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">

<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p><b>Warrior</b> (born <b>James Brian Hellwig</b>; June 16, 1959 â April 8, 2014) was an American <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling" title="Professional wrestling">professional wrestler</a>, who wrestled, among the others, under the ring name <b>The Ultimate Warrior</b> for the World Wrestling Federation (WWF, now <a href="/wiki/WWE" title="WWE">WWE</a>) from 1987 to 1991 and again in 1992 and 1996. During his 1998 stint in <a href="/wiki/World_Championship_Wrestling" title="World Championship Wrestling">World Championship Wrestling</a> (WCW), he was known as <b>The Warrior</b>.</p>
<p>While in the WWF, he became a <a href="/wiki/List_of_WWE_Intercontinental_Champions" title="List of WWE Intercontinental Champions">two-time</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WWE_Intercontinental_Champion" title="WWE Intercontinental Champion">WWF Intercontinental Heavyweight Champion</a> and won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WWE_World_Championship" title="WWE World Championship">WWF World Heavyweight Championship</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_WWE_World_Champions" title="List of WWE World Champions">once</a> when he pinned <a href="/wiki/Hulk_Hogan" title="Hulk Hogan">Hulk Hogan</a> in the main event at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_VI" title="WrestleMania VI">WrestleMania VI</a>, making him the first wrestler to hold both titles concurrently.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lilsboy_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lilsboy-3">[3]</a></sup> Warrior retired from professional wrestling in 1998 and embarked on a <a href="/wiki/Public_speaking" title="Public speaking">public speaking</a> career, but wrestled one final match in Spain in 2008.</p>
<p>Warrior died on April 8, 2014, at the age of 54 in Scottsdale, Arizona. Over the preceding three days he had been inducted into the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Hall_of_Fame" title="WWE Hall of Fame">WWE Hall of Fame</a>, appeared at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_XXX" title="WrestleMania XXX">WrestleMania XXX</a>, and made his final public appearance on <i><a href="/wiki/WWE_Raw" title="WWE Raw">Raw</a></i>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>Warrior was born in 1959 as James Brian Hellwig,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> in Crawfordsville, Indiana. He was the oldest of five children and was raised by his mother (along with, later, his stepfather) after his father left his family when he was 12. His father died at 57 and a grandfather had died at 52; Warrior himself would die at 54.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-caldwell_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-caldwell-5">[5]</a></sup> The family moved to Indiana, where he graduated from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Veedersburg" title="Veedersburg">Veedersburg</a>'s Fountain Central High School and attended <a href="/wiki/Indiana_State_University" title="Indiana State University">Indiana State University</a> for a year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Steele_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Steele-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Bodybuilding_career">Bodybuilding career</span></h2>
<p>Prior to his career in professional wrestling Hellwig was an amateur bodybuilder,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-7">[7]</a></sup> competing in a number of <a href="/wiki/National_Physique_Committee" title="National Physique Committee">NPC contests</a> and winning the 1984 NPC Mr. Georgia crown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Hellwig started training with weights when he was 11 years old and has described himself as "the small, insecure kid who wasn't into any sports".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-7">[7]</a></sup> He moved to California where, after seeing bodybuilder <a href="/wiki/Robby_Robinson_(bodybuilder)" title="Robby Robinson (bodybuilder)">Robby Robinson</a>, he decided to take up the sport. His first contest took place in Florida, where he placed 5th. Later, while he was attending <a href="/wiki/Life_University" title="Life University">Life University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Marietta,_Georgia" title="Marietta, Georgia">Marietta, Georgia</a>, he won the Junior Atlanta contest and placed 5th at the 1981 <a href="/wiki/Amateur_Athletic_Union" title="Amateur Athletic Union">AAU</a> Collegiate <a href="/wiki/AAU_Mr._America" title="AAU Mr. America">Mr. America</a>. In 1983, he won the AAU Coastal USA, before taking the Mr. Georgia title the following year. His last bodybuilding contest was 1985's Junior USAs, which was won by future IFBB Pro, Ron Love. Hellwig finished 5th.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1985, after spending six weeks in <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> training for a bodybuilding contest, he was invited to join a group of bodybuilders â Garland Donoho, Mark Miller, and <a href="/wiki/Sting_(wrestler)" title="Sting (wrestler)">Steve Borden</a> â to form a professional wrestling team. Warrior accepted the invitation and abandoned his bodybuilding career as well as his plans to become a <a href="/wiki/Chiropractic" title="Chiropractic">chiropractor</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Robinson_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Robinson-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_wrestling_career">Professional wrestling career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career_.281985.E2.80.931986.29">Early career (1985â1986)</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blade_Runners" title="Blade Runners">Blade Runners</a></div>
<p>Hellwig began his professional wrestling career as Jim "Justice" Hellwig of Powerteam USA, the group of bodybuilders trained by Red Bastien and Rick Bassman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Later, they wrestled as The Freedom Fighters (Hellwig was known as Justice and Borden was called Flash) in Memphis' Continental Wrestling Association under manager <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Mantel" title="Dutch Mantel">Dutch Mantel</a>. Hellwig and <a href="/wiki/Sting_(wrestler)" title="Sting (wrestler)">Steve Borden</a> (who would later have success as "Sting"), formed a <a href="/wiki/Tag_team" title="Tag team">tag team</a> called The Blade Runners; Hellwig was "Blade Runner Rock" and Borden was "Blade Runner Flash". Debuting in the Memphis, Tennessee-based <a href="/wiki/Continental_Wrestling_Association" title="Continental Wrestling Association">Continental Wrestling Association</a> (CWA) promotion, run by <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Jarrett" title="Jerry Jarrett">Jerry Jarrett</a>, the team played baby faces at first, but fans were actually slow to take to the hulking duo in a territory that had featured sympathetic "good guy tag teams" like the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rock_%27n%27_Roll_Express" title="Rock 'n' Roll Express">Rock 'n' Roll Express</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Fabulous_Ones" title="The Fabulous Ones">The Fabulous Ones</a>.</p>
<p>They were quickly turned heel as The Blade Runners. The Blade Runners went on to wrestle for the Mid-South Wrestling promotion, which became the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Wrestling_Federation_(Bill_Watts)" title="Universal Wrestling Federation (Bill Watts)">Universal Wrestling Federation</a> (UWF) in 1986. According to Joseph Laurinaitis (aka <a href="/wiki/Road_Warrior_Animal" title="Road Warrior Animal">Road Warrior Animal</a>), UWF owner <a href="/wiki/Bill_Watts" title="Bill Watts">Bill Watts</a> created the Blade Runners and the intent was to make them a parody of <a href="/wiki/The_Road_Warriors" title="The Road Warriors">The Road Warriors</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-roadwarriors2_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-roadwarriors2-14">[14]</a></sup> They were part of <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Gilbert_(wrestler)" title="Eddie Gilbert (wrestler)">Eddie Gilbert</a>'s Hotstuff International group, before disbanding in 1986 when Hellwig left the UWF.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Flynn2_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Flynn2-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Class_Championship_Wrestling_.281986.E2.80.931987.29">World Class Championship Wrestling (1986â1987)</span></h3>
<p>In 1986, Warrior debuted in the <a href="/wiki/Dallas" title="Dallas">Dallas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>-based <a href="/wiki/World_Class_Championship_Wrestling" title="World Class Championship Wrestling">World Class Championship Wrestling</a> (WCCW) promotion, where he wrestled for $50 a night. He has stated that he adopted the ring name "Dingo Warrior" after a member of the WCCW locker room remarked that he looked like "a warrior".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Robinson_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Robinson-10">[10]</a></sup> This stood in contrast with a claim made by Road Warrior Animal, who stated that the Dingo Warrior was a recreation of Warrior's Blade Runner gimmick and was an attempt to present himself as an offspring of <a href="/wiki/The_Road_Warriors" title="The Road Warriors">The Road Warriors</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-roadwarriors2_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-roadwarriors2-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Initially Warrior was still a heel in the territory, managed by <a href="/wiki/Gary_Hart_(wrestler)" title="Gary Hart (wrestler)">Gary Hart</a>, although he was cheered during a heel versus heel feud with WCWA World Heavyweight Champion <a href="/wiki/Rick_Rude" title="Rick Rude">Rick Rude</a> after the two fell out during a tag match. After switching managers to <a href="/wiki/Paul_Bearer" title="Paul Bearer">Percival Pringle III</a>, Warrior turned babyface permanently after a falling out with fellow Pringle proteges <a href="/wiki/Buzz_Sawyer" title="Buzz Sawyer">Buzz Sawyer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Matt_Osborne" title="Matt Osborne">Matt Borne</a> after a six-man tag match. Warrior formed a tag team with <a href="/wiki/Lance_Von_Erich" title="Lance Von Erich">Lance Von Erich</a>, and the duo began competing for the <a href="/wiki/WCWA_World_Tag_Team_Championship" title="WCWA World Tag Team Championship">WCWA World Tag Team Championship</a>. On November 17, 1986, Warrior and Von Erich defeated <a href="/wiki/George_Wells_(wrestler)" title="George Wells (wrestler)">Master Gee</a> (substituting for champion <a href="/wiki/Buzz_Sawyer" title="Buzz Sawyer">Buzz Sawyer</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Matt_Osborne" title="Matt Osborne">Matt Borne</a> to win the title. They held the Championship until December 1 of that year, when they lost to Al Madril and <a href="/wiki/Brian_Adias" title="Brian Adias">Brian Adias</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Duncan1_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Duncan1-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1987, Warrior began competing for the <a href="/wiki/NWA_Texas_Heavyweight_Championship" title="NWA Texas Heavyweight Championship">WCWA Texas Heavyweight Championship</a>, losing to <a href="/wiki/Bob_Bradley_(wrestler)" title="Bob Bradley (wrestler)">Bob Bradley</a> in a tournament final on January 12. He won the title from Bradley on February 2 of that year. The title was held up in April 1987 after Warrior left the WCCW. He was reinstated as champion upon returning, but vacated it once more upon resigning from WCCW to join the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Wrestling_Entertainment" title="World Wrestling Entertainment">World Wrestling Federation</a>, where he adopted the ring name Ultimate Warrior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Duncan2_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Duncan2-17">[17]</a></sup> Warrior began appearing on house shows in June and was initially billed as The Dingo Warrior in house card promos by <a href="/wiki/Gene_Okerlund" title="Gene Okerlund">Gene Okerlund</a>, but soon had his name modified. There is dispute over who created the Ultimate Warrior name. <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Prichard" title="Bruce Prichard">Bruce Prichard</a> stated that <a href="/wiki/Vince_McMahon" title="Vince McMahon">Vince McMahon</a> did not know what a "Dingo" Warrior was, but because there was the "Modern Day Warrior" <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kerry_von_Erich" title="Kerry von Erich">Kerry von Erich</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Road_Warriors" title="The Road Warriors">The Road Warriors</a> there should not be one more simple warrior, but the ultimate warrior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Warrior claims after one of his first matches, McMahon had him do a pretaped promo. It was there Vince said we want you to do Warrior, but we don't want Dingo. The Warrior then proceeded to cut the promo and stated that he was not this warrior or that warrior, he was The Ultimate Warrior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>Between 1987 and 1989, he appeared in several TV ads for Westway Ford, a car dealership in <a href="/wiki/Irving,_Texas" title="Irving, Texas">Irving, Texas</a>. Warrior interacted in full wrestling costume with Westway's wacky character, "Mean Joe Greed."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Wrestling_Federation">World Wrestling Federation</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_push_.281987.E2.80.931988.29">Early push (1987â1988)</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Ultimate_Warrior%27s_Arm.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2035" data-file-width="2757" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/The_Ultimate_Warrior%27s_Arm.jpg/220px-The_Ultimate_Warrior%27s_Arm.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/The_Ultimate_Warrior%27s_Arm.jpg/330px-The_Ultimate_Warrior%27s_Arm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/The_Ultimate_Warrior%27s_Arm.jpg/440px-The_Ultimate_Warrior%27s_Arm.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Ultimate_Warrior%27s_Arm.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Warrior was known for his high energy entrances</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hellwig joined the World Wrestling Federation (WWF) in June 1987. First competing on house shows under his Dingo Warrior moniker, he defeated a series of <a href="/wiki/Job_(professional_wrestling)" title="Job (professional wrestling)">jobbers</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Steve_Lombardi" title="Steve Lombardi">Steve Lombardi</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Barry_Horowitz" title="Barry Horowitz">Barry Horowitz</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Mike_Sharpe" title="Mike Sharpe">Mike Sharpe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> He made his television debut as The Ultimate Warrior on the October 25 episode of <i><a href="/wiki/WWF_Wrestling_Challenge" title="WWF Wrestling Challenge">Wrestling Challenge</a></i>, where he defeated another jobber, Terry Gibbs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1987results_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-1987results-25">[25]</a></sup> The Ultimate Warrior became known for his high-energy ring entrances, which featured him racing into the arena at full speed, bursting into the ring, and violently shaking the ropes up and down. He was also known for his distinctive pattern of face paint. After several months of defeating jobbers, he was pinned for the first time in the WWF by fellow WWF rookie/future rival <a href="/wiki/Rick_Rude" title="Rick Rude">Rick Rude</a> on December 28, 1987.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1988results_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-1988results-26">[26]</a></sup> In early 1988, Warrior entered into his first real WWF feud with fellow strongman <a href="/wiki/Hercules_(wrestler)" title="Hercules (wrestler)">Hercules Hernandez</a>. The two faced off on the February 7, 1988 airing of <i>Wrestling Challenge</i>, where Hercules was disqualified for using his steel chain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWFresults688_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-WWFresults688-27">[27]</a></sup> Warrior then grabbed a hold of the chain and in the midst of a tug of war over it snapped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWFresults688_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-WWFresults688-27">[27]</a></sup> This led to a match at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_IV" title="WrestleMania IV">WrestleMania IV</a>, where Warrior was victorious in his pay-per-view debut.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1988results_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-1988results-26">[26]</a></sup> Warrior lost twice by pinfall shortly thereafter: cleanly to <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_the_Giant" title="AndrÃ© the Giant">AndrÃ© the Giant</a> in April in Italy,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> and to <a href="/wiki/Dino_Bravo" title="Dino Bravo">Dino Bravo</a>, who put his feet on the ropes for leverage, in Montreal in June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> In the summer of 1988, he wrestled <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Heenan" title="Bobby Heenan">Bobby Heenan</a> in a series of <a href="/wiki/Weasel" title="Weasel">weasel</a> suit matches, in which Warrior won by sleeper hold.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Intercontinental_Heavyweight_Champion_.281988.E2.80.931990.29">Intercontinental Heavyweight Champion (1988â1990)</span></h4>
<p>Less than a year after his WWF television debut, Warrior, a surprise substitute for the injured <a href="/wiki/Brutus_Beefcake" title="Brutus Beefcake">Brutus Beefcake</a>, won the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Intercontinental_Championship" title="WWE Intercontinental Championship">Intercontinental Heavyweight Championship</a>, defeating <a href="/wiki/The_Honky_Tonk_Man" title="The Honky Tonk Man">The Honky Tonk Man</a> in a 27-second <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Squash_match" title="Squash match">squash match</a> at the inaugural <a href="/wiki/SummerSlam_(1988)" title="SummerSlam (1988)">SummerSlam</a> on August 29, 1988.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1988results_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-1988results-26">[26]</a></sup> As champion, he captained a team at <a href="/wiki/Survivor_Series_(1988)" title="Survivor Series (1988)">Survivor Series '88</a>, where he was the sole survivor, pinning <a href="/wiki/Ron_Bass_(wrestler)" title="Ron Bass (wrestler)">Outlaw Ron Bass</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greg_Valentine" title="Greg Valentine">Greg Valentine</a> in succession to win the match for his team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1988results_26-3"><a href="#cite_note-1988results-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>As 1989 began, Warrior entered a feud with <a href="/wiki/Rick_Rude" title="Rick Rude">Rick Rude</a> over the Intercontinental title. The feud was sparked at the 1989 <a href="/wiki/Royal_Rumble_(1989)" title="Royal Rumble (1989)">Royal Rumble</a>, where the two met in a "super posedown". After Warrior drew the support of the live crowd in their judging of the contest, Rude attacked Warrior and choked him with a steel bar. This led to a championship match at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_V" title="WrestleMania V">WrestleMania V</a>, where Rude pinned Warrior to win the title with the help of his manager <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Heenan" title="Bobby Heenan">Bobby Heenan</a>, who held down Warrior's foot from outside the ring as he was being pinned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1989results_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-1989results-30">[30]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/SummerSlam_(1989)" title="SummerSlam (1989)">SummerSlam</a>, Warrior defeated Rude to regain the title and become a two-time Intercontinental Heavyweight Champion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1989results_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-1989results-30">[30]</a></sup> Warrior then began a feud with <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_the_Giant" title="AndrÃ© the Giant">AndrÃ© the Giant</a>, leading to a number of house shows in which Warrior defeated Andre in short squash matches, establishing Warrior as a main event level talent. The feud culminated at <a href="/wiki/Survivor_Series_(1989)" title="Survivor Series (1989)">Survivor Series</a> where the two captained opposing teams. Warrior eliminated AndrÃ© by knocking him out of the ring, where he was counted out. Warrior was again the sole survivor, pinning <a href="/wiki/Arn_Anderson" title="Arn Anderson">Arn Anderson</a> and Bobby Heenan to win the match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1989results_30-2"><a href="#cite_note-1989results-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="WWF_World_Heavyweight_Champion_.281990.E2.80.931991.29">WWF World Heavyweight Champion (1990â1991)</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hogan_passes_torch.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="282" data-file-width="353" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/69/Hogan_passes_torch.jpg/220px-Hogan_passes_torch.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/69/Hogan_passes_torch.jpg/330px-Hogan_passes_torch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/6/69/Hogan_passes_torch.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hogan_passes_torch.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Hulk_Hogan" title="Hulk Hogan">Hulk Hogan</a> (left) endorsing The Ultimate Warrior after Warrior defeated him to win the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WWE_World_Championship" title="WWE World Championship">WWF World Heavyweight Championship</a> at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_VI" title="WrestleMania VI">WrestleMania VI</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Warrior received a push as WWF's main event successor to <a href="/wiki/Hulk_Hogan" title="Hulk Hogan">Hulk Hogan</a>, who had remained wrestling's biggest star throughout the 1980s. Following a few confrontations with Hogan, most notably at the 1990 <a href="/wiki/Royal_Rumble_(1990)" title="Royal Rumble (1990)">Royal Rumble</a>, the Warrior was written in as Hogan's opponent in the main event for <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_VI" title="WrestleMania VI">WrestleMania VI</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SkyDome" title="SkyDome">SkyDome</a> in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>. The match was billed as "The Ultimate Challenge", as both Hogan's <a href="/wiki/WWE_Championship" title="WWE Championship">WWF World Heavyweight Championship</a> and Warrior's Intercontinental Heavyweight Championship were on the line. Warrior pinned Hogan after a Warrior Splash to become the only wrestler to hold both championships simultaneously.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1990results_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-1990results-31">[31]</a></sup> Warrior vacated the Intercontinental Championship, as WWF rules prohibited a wrestler from holding both titles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>After WrestleMania, Warrior successfully defended the championship against <a href="/wiki/Tonga_Fifita" title="Tonga Fifita">Haku</a>, <a href="/wiki/Curt_Hennig" title="Curt Hennig">Mr. Perfect</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ted_DiBiase" title="Ted DiBiase">Ted DiBiase</a>. At <a href="/wiki/SummerSlam_(1990)" title="SummerSlam (1990)">SummerSlam</a>, he retained the title over Rick Rude in a steel cage match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1990results_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-1990results-31">[31]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Randy_Savage" title="Randy Savage">"Macho Man" Randy Savage</a> was also introduced as a potential rival after interfering in a <i><a href="/wiki/WWF_The_Main_Event" title="WWF The Main Event">The Main Event</a></i> title match at the behest of DiBiase.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Warrior was inserted into the feud between <a href="/wiki/The_Road_Warriors" title="The Road Warriors">The Legion of Doom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Demolition_(professional_wrestling)" title="Demolition (professional wrestling)">Demolition</a>, leading to victories for the Warrior and LOD in six-man tag team matches in house shows as well as the October 13, 1990 airing of <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night%27s_Main_Event" title="Saturday Night's Main Event">Saturday Night's Main Event</a></i>. The feud culminated at <a href="/wiki/Survivor_Series_(1990)" title="Survivor Series (1990)">Survivor Series</a>, where The Warriors (Ultimate Warrior, LOD and Kerry Von Erich) defeated The Perfect Team (Mr. Perfect and Demolition). For the third consecutive year, Warrior was the sole survivor for his team. He later survived the "Grand Finale Match of Survival" with Hulk Hogan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1990results_31-2"><a href="#cite_note-1990results-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Randy_Savage_vs_Ultimate_Warrior.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="379" data-file-width="606" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Randy_Savage_vs_Ultimate_Warrior.jpg/220px-Randy_Savage_vs_Ultimate_Warrior.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Randy_Savage_vs_Ultimate_Warrior.jpg/330px-Randy_Savage_vs_Ultimate_Warrior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Randy_Savage_vs_Ultimate_Warrior.jpg/440px-Randy_Savage_vs_Ultimate_Warrior.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Randy_Savage_vs_Ultimate_Warrior.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Warrior wrestling <a href="/wiki/Randy_Savage" title="Randy Savage">Randy Savage</a>, who he retired at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_VII" title="WrestleMania VII">WrestleMania VII</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In January 1991, Warrior faced <a href="/wiki/Sgt._Slaughter" title="Sgt. Slaughter">Sgt. Slaughter</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Rumble_(1991)" title="Royal Rumble (1991)">Royal Rumble</a>. Slaughter's <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gimmick_(professional_wrestler)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gimmick (professional wrestler) (page does not exist)">gimmick</a> at the time was a traitor who had betrayed America by aligning himself with an Iraqi (<a href="/wiki/Kayfabe" title="Kayfabe">kayfabe</a>) military general, <a href="/wiki/Adnan_Al-Kaissie" title="Adnan Al-Kaissie">General Adnan</a>. In the context of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Gulf War</a>, this made Slaughter one of the most hated heels at the time. After rejecting an earlier request to grant a title shot to Savage, <a href="/wiki/Sherri_Martel" title="Sherri Martel">Sensational Sherri</a> interjected herself in the Warrior's championship match to distract him. Her interference eventually led to a Savage sneak attack, where he struck Warrior over the head with a metal scepter and allowed Slaughter to pin Warrior to win the title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Flynn2_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Flynn2-15">[15]</a></sup> Warrior went on to feud with Savage, and the rivalry culminated in a "Career Ending" match at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_VII" title="WrestleMania VII">WrestleMania VII</a> which Warrior won, forcing Savage to retire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Various_feuds_and_departure_.281991.E2.80.931992.29">Various feuds and departure (1991â1992)</span></h4>
<p>The next chapter of Warrior's career was an encounter with <a href="/wiki/The_Undertaker" title="The Undertaker">The Undertaker</a>, after Undertaker and his manager, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Bearer" title="Paul Bearer">Paul Bearer</a>, locked Warrior in a coffin on the set of Bearer's <i>Funeral Parlor</i>. WWF officials worked feverishly to break the casket open, finally revealing Warrior's seemingly lifeless body, and the torn fabric inside of the coffin indicating Warrior's desperate struggle to get out. Warrior was finally revived by the officials performing <a href="/wiki/Cardiopulmonary_resuscitation" title="Cardiopulmonary resuscitation">CPR</a>. This led to <a href="/wiki/Jake_Roberts" title="Jake Roberts">Jake "The Snake" Roberts</a> offering to give Warrior "the knowledge of the dark side" in order to prepare Warrior to take his revenge on the Undertaker. This involved Roberts giving Warrior three "tests" shown on WWF TV in consecutive weeks. For the first test, Roberts locked Warrior inside of a coffin for a second time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-steelchair_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-steelchair-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>For the second test, Warrior was "buried alive" by Roberts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-steelchair_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-steelchair-34">[34]</a></sup> For the third test, the Warrior entered a room full of snakes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-steelchair_34-2"><a href="#cite_note-steelchair-34">[34]</a></sup> to find "the answer" in a chest in the middle of the room. Waiting inside the chest was a Spitting Cobra, which bit Warrior in the face. As Warrior weakened from the effects of the cobra's strike, Roberts made a heel turn and was joined by the Undertaker and Paul Bearer, revealing the three were working together all along. Roberts then uttered, "Never trust a snake."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-steelchair_34-3"><a href="#cite_note-steelchair-34">[34]</a></sup> The stage was now set for a feud between the Warrior and Roberts. The feud never took place, as Warrior was involved in an alleged pay dispute with WWF owner <a href="/wiki/Vince_McMahon" title="Vince McMahon">Vince McMahon</a> over the <a href="/wiki/SummerSlam_(1991)" title="SummerSlam (1991)">SummerSlam</a> main event, where Warrior was teamed with Hulk Hogan in a handicap match against Sgt. Slaughter, <a href="/wiki/The_Iron_Sheik" title="The Iron Sheik">Colonel Mustafa</a>, and General Adnan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>On July 10, 1991, Warrior sent a letter to Vince McMahon requesting inclusions in his new WWF contract. He wanted $550,000 for performing at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_VII" title="WrestleMania VII">WrestleMania VII</a>, a guaranteed number of working days, travel accommodations and a higher percentage of merchandise sales. He remarked that $550,000 "was fair", and that "[Warrior] meant as much or more to the show than Hulk [Hogan]". He ended his letter with "Whatever your decision, I can and will live with it. Till then I remain home with one who cares".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>The WWF responded on July 13, agreeing to $550,000 for WrestleMania VII, a higher royalty rate and promising no other WWF performer would be paid more than him on WWF pay per views. Vince McMahon personally ended the letter by saying, "I would like to express my deepest appreciation and admiration for you as a performer, as a member of the WWF family, as a man, and as my friend".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following WWF's annual <a href="/wiki/SummerSlam_(1991)" title="SummerSlam (1991)">SummerSlam</a> event, Warrior was handed a letter dated August 26, 1991, from Vince McMahon, saying Warrior was suspended effective immediately. Among other things, McMahon said, "You threatened to stay at home thereby not even appearing at Titan's major summer pay-per-view event SummerSlam. I had no choice but to accede to your exorbitant demands. This was a serious mistake on your part". McMahon later testified that the only reason the company agreed to the contract was to "acquiesce to his demands temporarily" to ensure Warrior would perform at the SummerSlam event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>Upon receiving the letter, Warrior refused the suspension and left the WWF. Warrior formally sent a letter of resignation to the WWF in October 1991. The WWF refused to accept the letter since Warrior was under contract until September 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>With Hulk Hogan about to leave WWF between mid-1992 and early-1993, McMahon contacted Warrior about returning. He made his comeback at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_VIII" title="WrestleMania VIII">WrestleMania VIII</a> (to rescue Hulk Hogan from a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_professional_wrestling_terms#B" title="List of professional wrestling terms">beat down</a> at the hands of <a href="/wiki/Sid_Eudy" title="Sid Eudy">Sid Justice</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_Wright_(wrestler)" title="Charles Wright (wrestler)">Papa Shango</a>). Upon his return, he received a degree of creative control over his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_professional_wrestling_terms#B" title="List of professional wrestling terms">bookings</a>. One storyline involved Papa Shango, a "<a href="/wiki/Witch_doctor" title="Witch doctor">witch doctor</a>", casting a spell over Warrior, causing him to convulse and <a href="/wiki/Vomiting" title="Vomiting">vomit</a> in very odd colors, though Warrior says he hated that story and had no control over it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Flynn2_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-Flynn2-15">[15]</a></sup> The Warrior was booked for a WWF World Heavyweight Championship match against then-champion, <a href="/wiki/Randy_Savage" title="Randy Savage">"Macho Man" Randy Savage</a> at <a href="/wiki/SummerSlam_(1992)" title="SummerSlam (1992)">SummerSlam</a> in August 1992. The Warrior won the match by countout, but not the title. In November 1992, Warrior was scheduled to team with Savage (as The Ultimate Maniacs) to face <a href="/wiki/Ric_Flair" title="Ric Flair">Ric Flair</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scott_Hall" title="Scott Hall">Razor Ramon</a> at <a href="/wiki/Survivor_Series_(1992)" title="Survivor Series (1992)">Survivor Series</a>. Weeks before the event, Warrior was released for disputed reasons and replaced by <a href="/wiki/Curt_Hennig" title="Curt Hennig">Mr. Perfect</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>The initial plan for Warrior's 1992 return was to eventually give him another run with the WWF World Heavyweight Championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ultimatelegend_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-ultimatelegend-44">[44]</a></sup> However, his return coincided with the government's crackdown on steroids in wrestling. Warrior was admittedly a heavy user of steroids during his professional wrestling career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-caldwell_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-caldwell-5">[5]</a></sup> In his book <i>Sex, Lies and Headlocks</i>, <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> writer <a href="/wiki/Shaun_Assael" title="Shaun Assael">Shaun Assael</a> stated that Canadian chemist <a href="/wiki/Mauro_Di_Pasquale" title="Mauro Di Pasquale">Mauro Di Pasquale</a>, who had been hired in June to monitor the WWF's new drug testing program and was known for being tough towards anyone who failed a drug test,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pppafmaro_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-pppafmaro-45">[45]</a></sup> nailed Warrior for steroid use in September and was able to successfully persuade McMahon, who was under federal scrutiny at the time for allegations of illegally supplying steroids to some of his wrestlers, to release Warrior from the company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pppafmaro_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-pppafmaro-45">[45]</a></sup> However, in the <i>Warrior: The Ultimate Legend</i> documentary Vince McMahon claims that it was Warrior's experimenting with <a href="/wiki/Growth_hormone" title="Growth hormone">growth hormone</a> which led to his departure; Warrior was suspended and in return would skip dates as he took offense to McMahon's actions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ultimatelegend_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-ultimatelegend-44">[44]</a></sup> Warrior left the company on November 21, 1992.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Semi-retirement_.281992.E2.80.931996.29">Semi-retirement (1992â1996)</span></h3>
<p>Between November 1992 and July 1995, Warrior was semi-retired. During his time away from the WWF, Warrior opened the short-lived "Warrior University", a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_professional_wrestling_terms#S" title="List of professional wrestling terms">professional wrestling school</a> based in <a href="/wiki/Scottsdale,_Arizona" title="Scottsdale, Arizona">Scottsdale, Arizona</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Torch_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Torch-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 1992, he wrestled as the Dingo Warrior against <a href="/wiki/Hercules_(wrestler)" title="Hercules (wrestler)">Hercules Hernandez</a> in Billerica, Massachusetts, for <a href="/wiki/Killer_Kowalski" title="Killer Kowalski">Killer Kowalski</a>'s International Wrestling Federation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In April 1993, he toured Europe for World Wrestlings Superstars and that same year he also played the role of "the swordsman" in the action movie <i>Firepower</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 1995, he returned to the ring for the National Wrestling Conference (NWC) promotion in Las Vegas, defeating <a href="/wiki/The_Honky_Tonk_Man" title="The Honky Tonk Man">The Honky Tonk Man</a>. He had also wrestled a tour of Europe for <a href="/wiki/Otto_Wanz" title="Otto Wanz">Otto Wanz</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Catch_Wrestling_Association" title="Catch Wrestling Association">Catch Wrestling Association</a> (CWA) promotion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Torch_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-Torch-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>On February 10, 1996, he defeated <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Garvin" title="Jimmy Garvin">Jimmy Garvin</a> in an independent show in Princeton, West Virginia.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_return_to_the_WWF_.281996.29">Second return to the WWF (1996)</span></h3>
<p>Warrior returned to the WWF on March 31, 1996, defeating <a href="/wiki/Triple_H" title="Triple H">Hunter Hearst Helmsley</a> at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_XII" title="WrestleMania XII">WrestleMania XII</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OWoW_1-6"><a href="#cite_note-OWoW-1">[1]</a></sup> He made his first appearance on <i><a href="/wiki/WWE_Raw" title="WWE Raw">Monday Night Raw</a></i> on April 8, where he gave an in-ring interview and credited the "voices" of the "warriors" (his name for members of the WWF audience) for his return; he was then interrupted by <a href="/wiki/Goldust" title="Goldust">Goldust</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PWInsider_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-PWInsider-48">[48]</a></sup> Warrior challenged for Goldust's Intercontinental Championship at <a href="/wiki/In_Your_House_7:_Good_Friends,_Better_Enemies" title="In Your House 7: Good Friends, Better Enemies">In Your House 7</a>; Warrior won the match by countout, but did not win the title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OWoW_1-7"><a href="#cite_note-OWoW-1">[1]</a></sup> The following night on <i>Monday Night Raw</i>, Warrior defeated <a href="/wiki/Kane_(wrestler)" title="Kane (wrestler)">Isaac Yankem, DDS</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OWoW_1-8"><a href="#cite_note-OWoW-1">[1]</a></sup> A rematch with Intercontinental Champion Goldust, on the May 27 episode of the show, ended in a double countout, thus eliminating both men from the tournament and eventually giving <a href="/wiki/Big_Van_Vader" title="Big Van Vader">Vader</a> a bye into the semi-finals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OWoW_1-9"><a href="#cite_note-OWoW-1">[1]</a></sup> Warrior defeated <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Lawler" title="Jerry Lawler">Jerry Lawler</a> at <a href="/wiki/King_of_the_Ring_(1996)" title="King of the Ring (1996)">King of the Ring</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OWoW_1-10"><a href="#cite_note-OWoW-1">[1]</a></sup> and defeated <a href="/wiki/Owen_Hart" title="Owen Hart">Owen Hart</a> by disqualification on the July 8 episode of <i>Monday Night Raw</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OWoW_1-11"><a href="#cite_note-OWoW-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Warrior was scheduled to team with <a href="/wiki/Shawn_Michaels" title="Shawn Michaels">Shawn Michaels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Johnson" title="Ahmed Johnson">Ahmed Johnson</a> to face Owen Hart, <a href="/wiki/Davey_Boy_Smith" title="Davey Boy Smith">Davey Boy Smith</a>, and Vader at <a href="/wiki/In_Your_House_9:_International_Incident" title="In Your House 9: International Incident">In Your House 9</a> later that month, but the WWF terminated Warrior's contract when he missed several house shows and taking time off allegedly to grieve the death of his father. WWF owner Vince McMahon claimed that Warrior had not seen his father in ten years and did not care much for him; therefore, he did not take Warrior's excuse for missing house shows at face value. Warrior disputes McMahon's explanation, claiming that the real reason why he no showed those events was a breach of contract by McMahon, in which WWF sold Warrior's merchandise without giving him a percentage. He was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Sid_Eudy" title="Sid Eudy">Sycho Sid</a> at In Your House 9.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PWInsider_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-PWInsider-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Championship_Wrestling_and_retirement_.281998.29">World Championship Wrestling and retirement (1998)</span></h3>
<p>WCW signed Warrior in 1998. He formed a <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_professional_wrestling_terms#Stable" title="Glossary of professional wrestling terms">stable</a> opposing Hollywood Hulk Hogan's <a href="/wiki/New_World_Order_(professional_wrestling)" title="New World Order (professional wrestling)">New World Order (nWo)</a>: the "One Warrior Nation". The acronym oWn (One Warrior Nation) was a play on the name nWo. Highlights of the storyline included Warrior <a href="/wiki/Kidnapping" title="Kidnapping">kidnapping</a> and "converting" <a href="/wiki/Brutus_Beefcake" title="Brutus Beefcake">The Disciple</a> and frequent instances of "magic smoke" knocking out all of the nWo members except for Hollywood Hogan and covering Warrior's movement through a trapdoor in the ring. The trapdoor was responsible for nearly paralyzing <a href="/wiki/Davey_Boy_Smith" title="Davey Boy Smith">Davey Boy Smith</a>, when he awkwardly fell on it during a match at Fall Brawl 98.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>Warrior only participated in three matches in WCW. The first was the <a href="/wiki/WarGames_match#1998" title="WarGames match">WarGames</a> match at <a href="/wiki/Fall_Brawl#1998" title="Fall Brawl">Fall Brawl</a>, where he competed as a member of Team WCW, competing against 8 other wrestlers for a shot at <a href="/wiki/Bill_Goldberg" title="Bill Goldberg">Goldberg</a>'s <a href="/wiki/WCW_World_Heavyweight_Championship" title="WCW World Heavyweight Championship">WCW World Heavyweight Championship</a> at <a href="/wiki/Halloween_Havoc#1998" title="Halloween Havoc">Halloween Havoc</a>. <a href="/wiki/Diamond_Dallas_Page" title="Diamond Dallas Page">Diamond Dallas Page</a> won the match by pinning <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Ray" title="Stevie Ray">Stevie Ray</a>. On <i><a href="/wiki/WCW_Monday_Nitro" title="WCW Monday Nitro">Monday Nitro</a></i>, he teamed with Sting to defeat Hogan and <a href="/wiki/Bret_Hart" title="Bret Hart">Bret Hart</a> by disqualification, a match in which he had little participation; he was tagged in for a short exchange with Hart, then singlehandedly chased several nWo members down the entry way, whipping them with Hogan's belt. The third was his loss to Hogan at Halloween Havoc, in what is considered by <a href="/wiki/Eric_Bischoff" title="Eric Bischoff">Eric Bischoff</a> to be one of the worst main event pay-per-view wrestling matches ever.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> In the Halloween Havoc match, the timing of the maneuvers and hits was poor; an arm injury that Warrior received at WarGames further slowed the action. An attempt to "blind" Warrior with a fireball backfired when Hogan faced complications igniting a piece of flash paper, causing the fire to go up in Hogan's face instead. The match came to an end when <a href="/wiki/Horace_Hogan" title="Horace Hogan">Horace Hogan</a> hit Warrior in the back with a chair while Eric Bischoff had referee <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nick_Hamilton" title="Nick Hamilton">Nick Patrick</a> distracted. Hogan then scored the pinfall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>WCW claimed that attempts were made to save the storyline though Warrior has claimed in interviews and convention appearances that the only reason he was brought back was so Hogan could get a win over Warrior in return for Hogan's WrestleMania job. Warrior's last appearance in WCW was on the November 9, 1998 episode of <i>Monday Nitro</i>, when he came to the rescue of The Disciple who was being attacked by members of The nWo. Warrior retired from wrestling that year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nu-Wrestling_Evolution_.282008.29">Nu-Wrestling Evolution (2008)</span></h3>
<p>After retiring in 1999, Warrior only wrestled one match after that in 2008, against <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Jordan" title="Orlando Jordan">Orlando Jordan</a> in <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, Spain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Warrior won the match and thus the Nu-Wrestling Evolution World Heavyweight Championship, but then immediately vacated the title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="WWE_Hall_of_Fame_.282013.E2.80.932014.29">WWE Hall of Fame (2013â2014)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:THE_Ultimate_Warrior_WWE_Hall_of_Fame_induction.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2036" data-file-width="1371" height="327" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/THE_Ultimate_Warrior_WWE_Hall_of_Fame_induction.jpg/220px-THE_Ultimate_Warrior_WWE_Hall_of_Fame_induction.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/THE_Ultimate_Warrior_WWE_Hall_of_Fame_induction.jpg/330px-THE_Ultimate_Warrior_WWE_Hall_of_Fame_induction.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/THE_Ultimate_Warrior_WWE_Hall_of_Fame_induction.jpg/440px-THE_Ultimate_Warrior_WWE_Hall_of_Fame_induction.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:THE_Ultimate_Warrior_WWE_Hall_of_Fame_induction.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Warrior makes a speech during his induction into the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Hall_of_Fame" title="WWE Hall of Fame">WWE Hall of Fame</a>, April 5, 2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On February 20, 2013, Warrior confirmed on his official YouTube channel that he would be making an appearance at <a href="/wiki/WrestleCon" title="WrestleCon">WrestleCon</a> at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_29" title="WrestleMania 29">WrestleMania 29</a> on April 7, 2013. In the same clip he spoke positively about <a href="/wiki/Vince_McMahon" title="Vince McMahon">Vince McMahon</a> for the first time on his channel. His appearance was so popular that a second print run of tickets had to be ordered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>On July 15, 2013, Warrior was featured in a <i><a href="/wiki/WWE_2K14" title="WWE 2K14">WWE 2K14</a></i> game trailer and revealed he was in the roster as a pre-order bonus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>On April 5, 2014, The Ultimate Warrior was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Hall_of_Fame" title="WWE Hall of Fame">WWE Hall of Fame</a> Class of 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWEHOF_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-WWEHOF-58">[58]</a></sup> The next day, Warrior appeared at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_XXX" title="WrestleMania XXX">WrestleMania XXX</a>, and the following night delivered a promo on <i><a href="/wiki/WWE_Raw" title="WWE Raw">Raw</a></i>, his first appearance on the show since his final WWF TV match in 1996.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> During what turned out to be his final public appearance, Warrior gave a speech to the fans and wrestlers past and present as his Ultimate Warrior character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>Warrior married Shari Lynn Tyree on October 2, 1982.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> They remained together for the majority of Warrior's WWF career before divorcing on March 22, 1991, two days before <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_VII" title="WrestleMania VII">WrestleMania VII</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Warrior married for the second time to Dana Viale on January 31, 1999. They had two daughters, Indiana (2000) and Mattigan (December 16, 2002).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Steele_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Steele-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_rumors">Death rumors</span></h3>
<p>Warrior returned to the WWF at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_VIII" title="WrestleMania VIII">WrestleMania VIII</a> after nearly eight months on hiatus after <a href="/wiki/SummerSlam_(1991)" title="SummerSlam (1991)">SummerSlam 1991</a>. Due to the drastic change in his appearance (shorter, blonder hair and a smaller physique), rumors began circulating that a new wrestler was playing the role. At the time it was rumored to be then-WWF contractor Kerry Von Erich. Some said Warrior died from <a href="/wiki/Liver_failure" title="Liver failure">liver failure</a> due to years of steroid abuse or that his signature arm tassels cut off his blood circulation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeathRumors_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-DeathRumors-63">[63]</a></sup> WWE claims that the theory that a different man returned to play The Ultimate Warrior at WrestleMania VIII remains "perhaps the longest standing urban legend in WWE history".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> WWE announcer <a href="/wiki/Tom_Phillips_(wrestling)" title="Tom Phillips (wrestling)">Tom Phillips</a> claims that the rumors likely originated from <a href="/wiki/Gene_Okerlund" title="Gene Okerlund">Gene Okerlund</a>'s WCW Hotline as well as the WCW debut of Warrior doppelgÃ¤nger <a href="/wiki/The_Renegade_(wrestler)" title="The Renegade (wrestler)">The Renegade</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trademark_and_libel_litigation">Trademark and libel litigation</span></h3>
<p>In 1993, Hellwig legally changed his name to the <a href="/wiki/Mononymous_person" title="Mononymous person">mononym</a> Warrior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> This one-word name appears on all legal documents pertaining to Warrior, and his children carry the Warrior name as their legal surname.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>Warrior and the WWF engaged in a series of lawsuits and legal actions in 1996 and 1998,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> where both parties sought a declaration that they owned the characters, Warrior and Ultimate Warrior, under both contract and copyright law. The court ruled that Warrior was legally entitled to use the gimmick, costuming, face paint designs, and mannerisms of the "Warrior" character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lilsboy_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lilsboy-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Flynn3_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Flynn3-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>On September 27, 2005, WWE released a DVD documentary focusing on Warrior's retrospective wrestling career, titled <i>The Self-Destruction of the Ultimate Warrior</i>. The DVD featured clips of his more notable feuds and matches along with commentary from WWE stars past and present (most of which are unflattering), with <a href="/wiki/Triple_H" title="Triple H">Triple H</a> (by this point one of WWE's top main eventers and the husband of Vince McMahon's daughter <a href="/wiki/Stephanie_McMahon" title="Stephanie McMahon">Stephanie McMahon</a>) adding that his WrestleMania debut loss against Warrior at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_XII" title="WrestleMania XII">WrestleMania XII</a> left him with mixed emotions, saying that Warrior "ruined the experience" for him and was "one of the most unprofessional guys" he's ever performed with.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> The DVD has provoked some controversy due to Warrior's own allegations of libel by WWE against him. Originally, Warrior was asked to help with the production of the DVD, but as he refused to work with WWE (citing he did not want to be associated with their <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling_promotion" title="Professional wrestling promotion">promotion</a>), there had been some resulting animosity between Warrior and WWE over the Warrior claiming bias on the part of WWE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sokol_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sokol-72">[72]</a></sup> In January 2006, Warrior filed another lawsuit against WWE in an <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a> court over the depiction of his wrestling career in <i>The Self-Destruction of the Ultimate Warrior</i> DVD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> On September 18, 2009, Warrior's lawsuit in Arizona was dismissed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Motivational_speaking">Motivational speaking</span></h3>
<p>Warrior formally retired from wrestling in 1999 and had a short-lived career as a <a href="/wiki/Conservatism" title="Conservatism">conservative</a> speaker and commentator, partnering with conservative spokesman Daniel Pinheiro, denouncing <a href="/wiki/Left-wing_politics" title="Left-wing politics">left-wing politics</a>. In one instance, he mentioned that "queering doesn't make the world work" during a speech at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Connecticut" title="University of Connecticut">University of Connecticut</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Warrior explained those comments on his website as meaning that the human race would die out if everyone were a <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homosexual</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lilsboy_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-Lilsboy-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Flynn4_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-Flynn4-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Writing">Writing</span></h3>
<p>In 1996, Warrior published a comic book titled <i>Warrior</i>, featuring himself as the main character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> The series was co-written with Jim Callahan and illustrated by the Sharp Brothers.</p>
<p>Warrior maintained a <a href="/wiki/Blog" title="Blog">blog</a> on his personal website titled "Warrior's Machete", where he discussed his personal life, his personal views on <a href="/wiki/Politics" title="Politics">politics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sexual_orientation" title="Sexual orientation">sexuality</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patriotism" title="Patriotism">patriotism</a>, and his legacy as a wrestler, amongst other topics. There were numerous instances where Warrior used his blog to address his viewpoint on members of his wrestling past (Vince McMahon, Road Warrior Animal, The British Bulldog, Owen Hart, Hulk Hogan, <a href="/wiki/Lex_Luger" title="Lex Luger">Lex Luger</a>);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> historical (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King,_Jr." title="Martin Luther King, Jr.">Martin Luther King</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a>) or religious figures (<a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Warrior depicted celebrities who were newsworthy at the time of his blog (<a href="/wiki/Heath_Ledger" title="Heath Ledger">Heath Ledger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paris_Hilton" title="Paris Hilton">Paris Hilton</a>). Warrior occasionally referenced his respect for the Founding Fathers of the United States, and also enjoyed books like Homer's <i>Odyssey</i> and James Allen's <i><a href="/wiki/As_a_Man_Thinketh" title="As a Man Thinketh">As a Man Thinketh</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> In 2012 he started selling "Weapons of Wisdom", inspirational 6Ã9 pieces of watercolor paper with drawings, quotes and doodles on them by the Warrior himself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> He also used the blog to post replies to letters from fans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Death">Death</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Ultimate_Warrior_RAW_April_2014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4272" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/The_Ultimate_Warrior_RAW_April_2014.jpg/220px-The_Ultimate_Warrior_RAW_April_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/The_Ultimate_Warrior_RAW_April_2014.jpg/330px-The_Ultimate_Warrior_RAW_April_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/The_Ultimate_Warrior_RAW_April_2014.jpg/440px-The_Ultimate_Warrior_RAW_April_2014.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Ultimate_Warrior_RAW_April_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Ultimate Warrior in his last appearance on <i><a href="/wiki/WWE_Raw" title="WWE Raw">Raw</a></i>, in a mask depicting his trademark face paint</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Warrior died on April 8, 2014 in Scottsdale, Arizona. He had been inducted into the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Hall_of_Fame" title="WWE Hall of Fame">WWE Hall of Fame</a> on April 5, appeared at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_XXX" title="WrestleMania XXX">WrestleMania XXX</a> on April 6, and made his first <i><a href="/wiki/WWE_Raw" title="WWE Raw">Raw</a></i> appearance in almost 18 years on April 7, the day before his death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-death_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-death-84">[84]</a></sup> According to reports, Warrior clutched his chest and collapsed at 5:50Â p.m. while walking to his car with his wife outside of their hotel in Arizona. He was rushed to the hospital where he was pronounced dead at age 54.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Warrior's colleagues said Warrior appeared frail during WrestleMania weekend, and said that he was sweating profusely and breathing heavily backstage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>An autopsy revealed Warrior died of a <a href="/wiki/Myocardial_infarction" title="Myocardial infarction">heart attack</a> caused by <a href="/wiki/Atherosclerosis" title="Atherosclerosis">atherosclerotic</a> <a href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_disease" title="Cardiovascular disease">cardiovascular disease</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Burial/cremation details still have not been released as of 2016.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Ultimate_Warrior_April_2014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1469" data-file-width="1009" height="320" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/The_Ultimate_Warrior_April_2014.jpg/220px-The_Ultimate_Warrior_April_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/The_Ultimate_Warrior_April_2014.jpg/330px-The_Ultimate_Warrior_April_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/The_Ultimate_Warrior_April_2014.jpg/440px-The_Ultimate_Warrior_April_2014.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Ultimate_Warrior_April_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Warrior's last public appearance took place on <i>Raw</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Although Warrior's relationship with WWE was strained at times,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> more recently WWE has recognized him as one of the legends of the company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWEWarrior_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-WWEWarrior-2">[2]</a></sup> WWE described him as being "As devastating and intense as any Superstar who stepped through the ropes...", further saying that "The Ultimate Warrior may be the most enigmatic man to ever hold the WWE Championship."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> In 2011, WWE called him "one of the most recognizable" wrestlers in WWE history, praising his ability to draw power from "the WWE Universe", and further spoke of his impact as having "brought <a href="/wiki/Hulk_Hogan#The_crowning_of_Hulkamania_.281983.E2.80.931984.29" title="Hulk Hogan">Hulkamania</a> to its knees" at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_VI" title="WrestleMania VI">WrestleMania VI</a>, "retired the <a href="/wiki/Randy_Savage" title="Randy Savage">Madness</a> at <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_VII" title="WrestleMania VII">WrestleMania VII</a> and press slammed a slew of the greatest legends of his era".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/WWE_All_Stars" title="WWE All Stars">WWE All Stars</a>, in which Ultimate Warrior appears as one of the Legends, WWE stated that he was the "ultimate archetype of strength and intensity", and further stated that "without question, the Ultimate Warrior has etched his name in the pantheon of WWE greats".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>Warrior appeared in the <a href="/wiki/Mattel" title="Mattel">Mattel</a> <a href="/wiki/WWE_Legends_action_figures_(Mattel)" title="WWE Legends action figures (Mattel)">Legends</a> figures line in both <a href="/wiki/WWE_Legends_action_figures_(Mattel)" title="WWE Legends action figures (Mattel)">Series 4</a> and <a href="/wiki/WWE_Legends_action_figures_(Mattel)" title="WWE Legends action figures (Mattel)">Series 6</a>. He was also chosen as one of six legends to be included in the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Legends_action_figures_(Mattel)" title="WWE Legends action figures (Mattel)">Defining Moments</a> series of action figures. Most recently he was one of a number of figures in the WWE Superstars line of Mattel action figures in an assortment called "World Champions". Warrior further appears as a playable legend in <i><a href="/wiki/WWE_All_Stars" title="WWE All Stars">WWE All Stars</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/WWE_Legends_of_WrestleMania" title="WWE Legends of WrestleMania">WWE Legends of WrestleMania</a></i>. The Ultimate Warrior was featured in <i><a href="/wiki/WWE_2K14" title="WWE 2K14">WWE 2K14</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/WWE_2K15" title="WWE 2K15">WWE 2K15</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/WWE_2K16" title="WWE 2K16">WWE 2K16</a></i>, and it was announced June 14, 2016 he will appear in <i><a href="/wiki/WWE_2K17" title="WWE 2K17">WWE 2K17</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> In 2005, WWE released <i>The Self-Destruction of The Ultimate Warrior</i> DVD, which portrayed Warrior in a negative light. Warrior claimed that if WWE wanted to induct him into the <a href="/wiki/WWE_Hall_of_Fame" title="WWE Hall of Fame">WWE Hall of Fame</a> they would have "to tell the right story" opposite of the one depicted in the 2005 DVD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> WWE released <i>Ultimate Warrior: The Ultimate Collection</i>, a 3-DVD, 540 minute-compilation of matches and stories, which portrayed Warrior far more positively, on April 1, 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Warrior was inducted into the WWE Hall of Fame on April 5, 2014, the night before <a href="/wiki/WrestleMania_XXX" title="WrestleMania XXX">WrestleMania XXX</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWEHOF_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-WWEHOF-58">[58]</a></sup>'</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dana_Warrior_Award.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2693" data-file-width="1515" height="391" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Dana_Warrior_Award.jpg/220px-Dana_Warrior_Award.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Dana_Warrior_Award.jpg/330px-Dana_Warrior_Award.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Dana_Warrior_Award.jpg/440px-Dana_Warrior_Award.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dana_Warrior_Award.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dana Warrior presents the inaugural Warrior Award in front of an Ultimate Warrior statue at the 2015 Hall of Fame ceremony</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Warrior had been largely alienated from his peers in professional wrestling in the decade before his death, and was sometimes described as a bitter man on bad terms with various wrestling figures such as <a href="/wiki/Vince_McMahon" title="Vince McMahon">Vince McMahon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hulk_Hogan" title="Hulk Hogan">Hulk Hogan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jake_Roberts" title="Jake Roberts">Jake Roberts</a>. With Warrior's reconciling with the professional wrestling industry just before his death, some of his former adversaries offered their condolences. McMahon stated that "We are all so sad that the Ultimate Warrior has passed away. Our heart is with his wife Dana and his two daughters." Hogan said, "RIP WARRIOR. only love ... We talked, both forgave each other, we hugged, we shook hands as we told each other I love you, I am so sad, God bless his beautiful family". Roberts said that he was "Deeply saddened. We just had a great talk &amp; buried a senseless hatchet. Talked working together. RIP Warrior. Taking solace we made peace." News of his death spread the next day on sites such as Bing, Facebook, and Twitter. It was also mentioned on ABC News, HLN and CNN.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Reportedly almost immediately after Warrior's death, WWE sent two senior officials to Arizona to assist his widow in handling personal things such as grocery shopping so that she can focus on being with her and Warrior's daughters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>WWE paid tribute to Warrior on the April 14 episode of <i>Raw</i> with a ten bell salute and a video.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/WWE_Network" title="WWE Network">WWE Network</a> aired a lineup dubbed "Warrior Week" in Warrior's memory. The lineup included a four-part special.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> A wrestling themed episode of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Goldbergs_(TV_series)" title="The Goldbergs (TV series)">The Goldbergs</a></i>, which aired on May 6, was dedicated in Warrior's memory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> The 2015 film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Flintstones_%26_WWE:_Stone_Age_SmackDown!" title="The Flintstones &amp; WWE: Stone Age SmackDown!">The Flintstones &amp; WWE: Stone Age SmackDown!</a></i>, which stars <i><a href="/wiki/The_Flintstones" title="The Flintstones">The Flintstones</a></i> and WWE Superstars and <a href="/wiki/WWE_Diva" title="WWE Diva">Divas</a>, was dedicated to Warrior's memory.</p>
<p>At the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UFC_Fight_Night_40" title="UFC Fight Night 40">UFC Fight Night 40</a></i> weigh-ins, fighter <a href="/wiki/Lorenz_Larkin" title="Lorenz Larkin">Lorenz Larkin</a> wore an Ultimate Warrior mask, tassels and wristbands as a tribute.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>Warrior was awarded a posthumous <a href="/wiki/Slammy_Award" title="Slammy Award">Slammy Award</a> for Return of the Year in December 2014. A WWE-sponsored biography, entitled <i>Ultimate Warrior: A Life Lived Forever: The Legend of a WWE Hero</i>, was released in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>WWE also followed through with his request of adding a category into the WWE Hall of Fame by establishing the Warrior Award in his honor which will be given annually to honor WWE employees behind the scenes. The first recipient of the Warrior Award was a young fan named <a href="/wiki/Connor_Michalek" title="Connor Michalek">Connor Michalek</a>. In April 2016, <a href="/wiki/Joan_Lunden" title="Joan Lunden">Joan Lunden</a> was honored as the recipient of the 2016 Warrior Award.</p>
